Focaccia (esp. sourdough wheat, salt & pepper) is outstanding. Their sourdough bread loaf with sesame is equally good, but only because the charcoal they add is chemically inert (so tasteless). What's with all the dietary charcoal, California? It's weird. They make small loaves of while grain bread with neat inclusions, like shallots and mushrooms, olives and pecorino cheese, brie and sour cherry, sage and garlic, etc. It's pricey though; expect to spend about $10 a loaf. They sell by portions.< /Text>

<user>114934458726014833775</user>< Name>
Michael Cheung<//Name>
<time>1552709907917</time><Rate>4</Rate><text>TLDR: A small, local bakery with quite a bit of variety. They have some exceptional baked goods that left me wanting more. I would recommend going if you're in the area.

This place was not on my radar at all, it being so far away from the commercial area. I was introduced to this place by my brother, who goes around San Francisco and tries out many of the bakeries in the city. The bakery is not the easiest to see when passing by, it being fairly small. Upon entering, the first thing you see is the pastry case housing all of the baked goods that they have produced for the day. Directly behind the counter, there are people in the back working, making the baked goods, so there is a continuous stream of bread and pastries to be sold. As you focus your attention to the left, there is the register where you make your order, pay, and receive your order. I got a chicken empanada, warmed, and a hot cross.

When the lady on register asked if I wanted my empanada warmed, she asked if I wanted to warm it by oven for one minute or oven for seven minutes. I wasn't listening that attentively so I asked her to repeat it, which she did and I didn't understand the difference. After a small back and forth and her becoming slightly frustrated, I realized she misspoke and meant to say microwave. All this to say, you can either microwave or bake the empanada. She gave me my hot cross and I sat down on one of the tables to wait for my empanada to be heated.

The hot cross was amazing and nothing like what I was expecting. The pastry looks like a scone, but it is nothing like a scone at all. It is unexpectedly soft, much like bread. The bun (I would say it resembles a bun) has dried fruits in it, raisins and dried orange peels. The two dried fruit created a combination of both sweet and tangy that worked well together. The cross on the top was some kind of icing, that overall added to the sweetness of the bun. It was very good, to the point that I bought a second one when I was leaving.

After waiting the six minutes, the empanada was finished and it was good. The crust of the empanada was very flaky and it broke apart easily in my mouth. The stuffing inside was well seasoned, the chicken was flavorful and the corn was a plus. Overall though, it was nothing special about it. As for the bakery as a whole, they're pretty good. I felt the lady on the counter was a bit rude, but she was most likely working since the morning and was flustered. The empanada was alright, but, as stated before, nothing special. The hot cross, however, was absolutely delightful and were pretty must sold out by the time I was leaving, yearning for a second one. If I am every in the area, I would go back to try some more things there.</text><Pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPtz99wu3H_Zo0r4oQdF_8kO8UPOfcRTd3FLjKM=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPFLzRWrERO63nvAaWs386kLkC9Iwlb-BT8s5W3=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipP670o3x_tb5psgCW6RfVJAeB8ZvJjyjUzfKcDN=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pictures>< Resp>

It's great that they send you daily report cards with updates and pictures on how your dog is doing since I'll admit, I had a hard time leaving her and was worried about how she would do. < text>
Don't let the simple decor or the cheap red and white checkerboard picnic tablecloths fool you. This place definitely feels like a hidden gem of a restaurant. The lunch special is available seven days a week and the price to portion ratio for dine-in was superb. Fresh broccoli chicken and chow mein, I don't think I've seen such a large helping of delicious, tender chicken.

I don't have experience with either the owner or the take-out, but for a quiet lunch in the middle of a rainy Saturday, a mid-day meal for two of us filled bellies and was delightfully relaxing.<//text>

< Name>
Derrick Spears</Name>
<pics>None<//pics>< review>
I had a very enjoyable meal from Sky Dragon Restaurant.
I had a nice spread ordered for the evening consisting of egg rolls, hot and sour soup, BBQ pork, black bean chicken, orange beef, chow mein, and these little crab puff things.
The egg rolls were crisp.  The hot and sour soup was tasty and not too thick, which is a problem with a lot of restaurants I try.
The entrees were good!  I was especially pleased with the orange beef.  It was very good, not greasy, or bland, or dry, like many places I've eaten at.  The black bean chicken was spot on, as was the BBQ pork, so good with the snow peas!
The chowmein was perfect.  Nice and tender, soft and moist, but not soggy.  So many places have noodles that are dry and stringy.
The crab puff was good, too, but I've never had those before, so I can't compare.
Overall, this was a nice surprise for the day.  I was so sick of the local options closest to me.  If I had to eat one more greasy, overcooked and undercooked, poorly prepared, mushy meal that tasted of cornstarch and failure I was prepared to just give up on local Chinese food!  I'm glad I tried Sky Dragon!< /review>

<text>I am in middle school, and I find this site very useful! If you have a Clever account, but forgot your login for BrainPop or Canvas, you can easily sign in through Clever.  Looking at other people's reviews has shown me that many of the bad reviews are just because they dislike doing school work and getting it done. She made it a point when she went to the door that if I had a quarter she wouldn't have to come over and use the key to open the door for me! She seemed to be too wrapped up with whatever she was doing and it looked like it was some kind of paperwork! All she had to do was just either give me a token or open the door as she did!

Afterwards, I came to the counter to purchase some food! Mary Lou, was there but asked her fellow employee to take my order. Although she was there at the register she didn't want to assist me!
